# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
Introduction to Combustion Challenges in fire
bridging the scale gap


 ^J8ofLqhx

bridge gap => fundamental combustion
-> diffusion flames -> real fires ^UoDUHYL9

state of art in fire science to not advance as fast as other combustion

difficulties specific to fire: fueles- condensed-phase-unknown composition, composites, complex geometry
conditions, variable, unsteady, flow, thermal, evolving fueld. ^Qh8V5wPH

Why diffusion flames?
- Dominant combustion mode in real applications
- present everywhere, we can make experiments with burners
and control the boundary conditions
- radiating and sooting: governs heat transfer in fires and flames
- Research Challenge: coupling of mixing, chemestry, buoyancy, radiation


SCALE GAP ^dMNWtE4p

Thermal plume
- convective transport of mass and energy
- firebrand transport at long distance can cause spotting ignition

macroscopic  scale

mesoscopic scale
- porus media
- fuel substrate
- ignition

condense pahse
- heat and mass transfer 
- fuel ungergoes subsequent process
- global reaction

microscopic slace
- combustion reaction
- oxygen transport
soot porduction process
viscous dissipation ^E7UZtJb9

Canonical Diffusion flames

- Counterflow Flames
isolates strain/mixing thin difussion flames for kinetics & radiation studies

- Coflow
Isolates axisymmetric mixing with soot & radiation, ideal for validation

Oscillating Flames
Usa a skpeaker to get osscilations, gateway to turbalence regimies

Pool Fire ^1bSaysju

simplified model

- opposed jets
- laminar, 1D, strain-controlled: Isolates mixing vs chemestry
- bounary condition: yi(z=0-) = y_if, Y_i(z=L+) = Y_i0
- Characteristics scale


COFLOW diffusion flame
- geometry: vertical axisymmetric burner with inner fuel jet.
- steady, laminar diffusion flames: stabilized by the surronding coflow
- Dominant Processes: buoyancy, diffusion, radiation and soot formation
- Measured quantities.
- Transport equations.


POOL FIRE
- buoyancy dominated
- three main zones: perisistent basse, interminttent flame and smoke
- coupled processes: evaporation, radiation, soot.
- Key parameters: T,u, f_v, height, M, Q.
- revelande: large scale analog of coflow flames-.
- experiments with different fuels: heptane, ethylene, methanol pool, methanes, etc.

WILDFIRES
- driven by wind, terrain, and fuel heterogenity
- combines surface, crown, and ember driven flame spread.
- radiation, convectino, and embers ignites new fronts.
- coupled scales: turbulence, ...



WHO TO BRIDGE THE GAP?
- Each configuration isolates key physical mechanisms.
- Complexity Grows
- Work with dimensionless numbers.
Re, Pr,Da,Le,Ka,Ma,Pr,Sc.

RADIATION-SOOT-TEMPERATURE COUPLING

- there are highly non linear feedback on the equations.
- temperature field affect the chemestry.
- temper-> absorption k(f_s,T) affects RTE -> daitative cooling through divergence q_r -> affects T


BRIDGING THE SCALE GAP:




 ^Iv731ttX

BENCH-SCALE FLAMMABILITY TESTING

- Experimental testing to increase our fundamental understandting in fires
- SOTA: large scale tests pose disadvantages (high cost, repeatability resolution)
- IFIT, scala burner, simulador parrilla perfecta (C. Torres).
- Canonical flames: isolates specific physics
- Bridging the scale mean preserving these coupling not merely enalrging geometry


how experiments, simulations, and PIML close this gap


HOW THE SCHOOL BRIDGES SCALES?

- pipeline

1. EXperiments
coflow, pool, diagnostics

2. Inference & PIML
conventional, NNs, impose all phy knowledge we have

3. Reduced Models
Soot, radiation, DeepONet, solver to adapt to different scenarios.

4. CFD/LES
Validated, canonicals

5. Scenarios
Industrial/Fire ^286cH4KU

Piline V2
1. experiments: RGB/MS, radiance, T/f_v

2. Inference/ PIML
inverse mode PINN

3. Clousures/ Reduced Models

4. CFD/LES
RTE(particupating medio) subgrig & radiation

5. Scenarios rifes

 ^Lw6VmRr5

WHERE AI FITS?
- feed with data, and physic that we know from the problem
- is fast, help bridge data and physics: network
- interpretability with inverse mode PINN ~ XAI

 ^4hc1UItn

- we need less data because equations helps
- expose physical insight
- remain valid beyond training
- Is try to combine the best of 2 worlds :p ^sAnxf5Qg

SOME WORK FROM THE EC2G (energy & combustion Group)
- Experimental Platform
- Data Processing Pipeline
 1. Raw data
2. calibration, convert raw to phy unit.
3. region of interest, data filtred
4. data treatment.
...
